     1	/// The number of nanoseconds per millisecond.$
     2	pub const NSEC_PER_MSEC: i64 = bindings::NSEC_PER_MSEC as i64;$
$
     3	/// The time unit of Linux kernel. One jiffy equals (1/HZ) second.$
     4	pub type Jiffies = core::ffi::c_ulong;$
$
     5	/// The millisecond time unit.$
     6	pub type Msecs = core::ffi::c_uint;$
$
     7	/// Converts milliseconds to jiffies.$
     8	#[inline]$
     9	pub fn msecs_to_jiffies(msecs: Msecs) -> Jiffies {$
    10	    // SAFETY: The `__msecs_to_jiffies` function is always safe to call no$
    11	    // matter what the argument is.$
    12	    unsafe { bindings::__msecs_to_jiffies(msecs) }$
    13	}$
$
    14	/// A Rust wrapper around a `ktime_t`.$
    15	#[repr(transparent)]$
    16	#[derive(Copy, Clone)]$
    17	pub struct Ktime {$
    18	    inner: bindings::ktime_t,$
    19	}$
$
    20	impl Ktime {$
    21	    /// Create a `Ktime` from a raw `ktime_t`.$
    22	    #[inline]$
    23	    pub fn from_raw(inner: bindings::ktime_t) -> Self {$
    24	        Self { inner }$
    25	    }$
$
    26	    /// Get the current time using `CLOCK_MONOTONIC`.$
    27	    #[inline]$
    28	    pub fn ktime_get() -> Self {$
    29	        // SAFETY: It is always safe to call `ktime_get` outside of NMI context.$
    30	        Self::from_raw(unsafe { bindings::ktime_get() })$
    31	    }$
$
    32	    /// Divide the number of nanoseconds by a compile-time constant.$
    33	    #[inline]$
    34	    fn divns_constant<const DIV: i64>(self) -> i64 {$
    35	        self.to_ns() / DIV$
    36	    }$
$
    37	    /// Returns the number of nanoseconds.$
    38	    #[inline]$
    39	    pub fn to_ns(self) -> i64 {$
    40	        self.inner$
    41	    }$
$
    42	    /// Returns the number of milliseconds.$
    43	    #[inline]$
    44	    pub fn to_ms(self) -> i64 {$
    45	        self.divns_constant::<NSEC_PER_MSEC>()$
    46	    }$
    47	}$
$
    48	/// Returns the number of milliseconds between two ktimes.$
    49	#[inline]$
    50	pub fn ktime_ms_delta(later: Ktime, earlier: Ktime) -> i64 {$
    51	    (later - earlier).to_ms()$
    52	}$
$
    53	impl core::ops::Sub for Ktime {$
    54	    type Output = Ktime;$
$
    55	    #[inline]$
    56	    fn sub(self, other: Ktime) -> Ktime {$
    57	        Self {$
    58	            inner: self.inner - other.inner,$
    59	        }$
    60	    }$
    61	}$
    62	// SAFETY: This file is known to not have any active `fdget_pos` calls that did not take the$
    63	// `f_pos_lock` mutex, so it is safe to transfer it between threads.$
    64	unsafe impl Send for File {}$
$
    65	// SAFETY: This file is known to not have any active `fdget_pos` calls that did not take the$
    66	// `f_pos_lock` mutex, so it is safe to access its methods from several threads in parallel.$
    67	unsafe impl Sync for File {}$
$
    68	// SAFETY: The type invariants guarantee that `File` is always ref-counted. This implementation$
    69	// makes `ARef<File>` own a normal refcount.$
    70	unsafe impl AlwaysRefCounted for File {$
    71	    #[inline]$
    72	    fn inc_ref(&self) {$
    73	        // SAFETY: The existence of a shared reference means that the refcount is nonzero.$
    74	        unsafe { bindings::get_file(self.as_ptr()) };$
    75	    }$
$
    76	    #[inline]$
    77	    unsafe fn dec_ref(obj: ptr::NonNull<File>) {$
    78	        // SAFETY: To call this method, the caller passes us ownership of a normal refcount, so we$
    79	        // may drop it. The cast is okay since `File` has the same representation as `struct file`.$
    80	        unsafe { bindings::fput(obj.cast().as_ptr()) }$
    81	    }$
    82	}$
    83	pub struct RBTree<K, V> {$
    84	    root: bindings::rb_root,$
    85	    _p: PhantomData<Node<K, V>>,$
    86	}$
$
    87	// SAFETY: An [`RBTree`] allows the same kinds of access to its values that a struct allows to its$
    88	// fields, so we use the same Send condition as would be used for a struct with K and V fields.$
    89	unsafe impl<K: Send, V: Send> Send for RBTree<K, V> {}$
$
    90	// SAFETY: An [`RBTree`] allows the same kinds of access to its values that a struct allows to its$
    91	// fields, so we use the same Sync condition as would be used for a struct with K and V fields.$
    92	unsafe impl<K: Sync, V: Sync> Sync for RBTree<K, V> {}$
$
    93	impl<K, V> RBTree<K, V> {$
    94	    /// Creates a new and empty tree.$
    95	    pub fn new() -> Self {$
    96	        Self {$
    97	            // INVARIANT: There are no nodes in the tree, so the invariant holds vacuously.$
    98	            root: bindings::rb_root::default(),$
    99	            _p: PhantomData,$
   100	        }$
   101	    }$
$
   102	    /// Returns an iterator over the tree nodes, sorted by key.$
   103	    pub fn iter(&self) -> Iter<'_, K, V> {$
   104	        Iter {$
   105	            _tree: PhantomData,$
   106	            // INVARIANT:$
   107	            //   - `self.root` is a valid pointer to a tree root.$
   108	            //   - `bindings::rb_first` produces a valid pointer to a node given `root` is valid.$
   109	            iter_raw: IterRaw {$
   110	                // SAFETY: by the invariants, all pointers are valid.$
   111	                next: unsafe { bindings::rb_first(&self.root) },$
   112	                _phantom: PhantomData,$
   113	            },$
   114	        }$
   115	    }$
$
   116	    /// Returns a mutable iterator over the tree nodes, sorted by key.$
   117	    pub fn iter_mut(&mut self) -> IterMut<'_, K, V> {$
   118	        IterMut {$
   119	            _tree: PhantomData,$
   120	            // INVARIANT:$
   121	            //   - `self.root` is a valid pointer to a tree root.$
   122	            //   - `bindings::rb_first` produces a valid pointer to a node given `root` is valid.$
   123	            iter_raw: IterRaw {$
   124	                // SAFETY: by the invariants, all pointers are valid.$
   125	                next: unsafe { bindings::rb_first(from_mut(&mut self.root)) },$
   126	                _phantom: PhantomData,$
   127	            },$
   128	        }$
   129	    }$
$
   130	    /// Returns an iterator over the keys of the nodes in the tree, in sorted order.$
   131	    pub fn keys(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &'_ K> {$
   132	        self.iter().map(|(k, _)| k)$
   133	    }$
$
   134	    /// Returns an iterator over the values of the nodes in the tree, sorted by key.$
   135	    pub fn values(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &'_ V> {$
   136	        self.iter().map(|(_, v)| v)$
   137	    }$
$
   138	    /// Returns a mutable iterator over the values of the nodes in the tree, sorted by key.$
   139	    pub fn values_mut(&mut self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &'_ mut V> {$
   140	        self.iter_mut().map(|(_, v)| v)$
   141	    }$
$
   142	    /// Returns a cursor over the tree nodes, starting with the smallest key.$
   143	    pub fn cursor_front(&mut self) -> Option<Cursor<'_, K, V>> {$
   144	        let root = addr_of_mut!(self.root);$
   145	        // SAFETY: `self.root` is always a valid root node$
   146	        let current = unsafe { bindings::rb_first(root) };$
   147	        NonNull::new(current).map(|current| {$
   148	            // INVARIANT:$
   149	            // - `current` is a valid node in the [`RBTree`] pointed to by `self`.$
   150	            Cursor {$
   151	                current,$
   152	                tree: self,$
   153	            }$
   154	        })$
   155	    }$
$
   156	    /// Returns a cursor over the tree nodes, starting with the largest key.$
   157	    pub fn cursor_back(&mut self) -> Option<Cursor<'_, K, V>> {$
   158	        let root = addr_of_mut!(self.root);$
   159	        // SAFETY: `self.root` is always a valid root node$
   160	        let current = unsafe { bindings::rb_last(root) };$
   161	        NonNull::new(current).map(|current| {$
   162	            // INVARIANT:$
   163	            // - `current` is a valid node in the [`RBTree`] pointed to by `self`.$
   164	            Cursor {$
   165	                current,$
   166	                tree: self,$
   167	            }$
   168	        })$
   169	    }$
   170	}$
$
   171	impl<K, V> RBTree<K, V>$
   172	where$
   173	    K: Ord,$
   174	{$
   175	    /// Tries to insert a new value into the tree.$
   176	    ///$
   177	    /// It overwrites a node if one already exists with the same key and returns it (containing the$
   178	    /// key/value pair). Returns [`None`] if a node with the same key didn't already exist.$
   179	    ///$
   180	    /// Returns an error if it cannot allocate memory for the new node.$
   181	    pub fn try_create_and_insert($
   182	        &mut self,$
   183	        key: K,$
   184	        value: V,$
   185	        flags: Flags,$
   186	    ) -> Result<Option<RBTreeNode<K, V>>> {$
   187	        Ok(self.insert(RBTreeNode::new(key, value, flags)?))$
   188	    }$
$
   189	    /// Inserts a new node into the tree.$
   190	    ///$
   191	    /// It overwrites a node if one already exists with the same key and returns it (containing the$
   192	    /// key/value pair). Returns [`None`] if a node with the same key didn't already exist.$
   193	    ///$
   194	    /// This function always succeeds.$
   195	    pub fn insert(&mut self, node: RBTreeNode<K, V>) -> Option<RBTreeNode<K, V>> {$
   196	        match self.raw_entry(&node.node.key) {$
   197	            RawEntry::Occupied(entry) => Some(entry.replace(node)),$
   198	            RawEntry::Vacant(entry) => {$
   199	                entry.insert(node);$
   200	                None$
   201	            }$
   202	        }$
   203	    }$
$
   204	    fn raw_entry(&mut self, key: &K) -> RawEntry<'_, K, V> {$
   205	        let raw_self: *mut RBTree<K, V> = self;$
   206	        // The returned `RawEntry` is used to call either `rb_link_node` or `rb_replace_node`.$
   207	        // The parameters of `bindings::rb_link_node` are as follows:$
   208	        // - `node`: A pointer to an uninitialized node being inserted.$
   209	        // - `parent`: A pointer to an existing node in the tree. One of its child pointers must be$
   210	        //          null, and `node` will become a child of `parent` by replacing that child pointer$
   211	        //          with a pointer to `node`.$
   212	        // - `rb_link`: A pointer to either the left-child or right-child field of `parent`. This$
   213	        //          specifies which child of `parent` should hold `node` after this call. The$
   214	        //          value of `*rb_link` must be null before the call to `rb_link_node`. If the$
   215	        //          red/black tree is empty, then itM-bM-^@M-^Ys also possible for `parent` to be null. In$
   216	        //          this case, `rb_link` is a pointer to the `root` field of the red/black tree.$
   217	        //$
   218	        // We will traverse the tree looking for a node that has a null pointer as its child,$
   219	        // representing an empty subtree where we can insert our new node. We need to make sure$
   220	        // that we preserve the ordering of the nodes in the tree. In each iteration of the loop$
   221	        // we store `parent` and `child_field_of_parent`, and the new `node` will go somewhere$
   222	        // in the subtree of `parent` that `child_field_of_parent` points at. Once$
   223	        // we find an empty subtree, we can insert the new node using `rb_link_node`.$
   224	        let mut parent = core::ptr::null_mut();$
   225	        let mut child_field_of_parent: &mut *mut bindings::rb_node =$
   226	            // SAFETY: `raw_self` is a valid pointer to the `RBTree` (created from `self` above).$
   227	            unsafe { &mut (*raw_self).root.rb_node };$
   228	        while !(*child_field_of_parent).is_null() {$
   229	            let curr = *child_field_of_parent;$
   230	            // SAFETY: All links fields we create are in a `Node<K, V>`.$
   231	            let node = unsafe { container_of!(curr, Node<K, V>, links) };$
$
   232	            // SAFETY: `node` is a non-null node so it is valid by the type invariants.$
   233	            match key.cmp(unsafe { &(*node).key }) {$
   234	                // SAFETY: `curr` is a non-null node so it is valid by the type invariants.$
   235	                Ordering::Less => child_field_of_parent = unsafe { &mut (*curr).rb_left },$
   236	                // SAFETY: `curr` is a non-null node so it is valid by the type invariants.$
   237	                Ordering::Greater => child_field_of_parent = unsafe { &mut (*curr).rb_right },$
   238	                Ordering::Equal => {$
   239	                    return RawEntry::Occupied(OccupiedEntry {$
   240	                        rbtree: self,$
   241	                        node_links: curr,$
   242	                    })$
   243	                }$
   244	            }$
   245	            parent = curr;$
   246	        }$
$
   247	        RawEntry::Vacant(RawVacantEntry {$
   248	            rbtree: raw_self,$
   249	            parent,$
   250	            child_field_of_parent,$
   251	            _phantom: PhantomData,$
   252	        })$
   253	    }$
